<p>Kraków's historic centre, which includes <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w_Old_Town" title="Kraków Old Town">the Old Town</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kazimierz" title="Kazimierz">Kazimierz</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Wawel_Castle" title="Wawel Castle">Wawel Castle</a>, was included as the first of its kind on the list of UNESCO <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Sites</a> in 1978.<sup id="cite_ref-Cracow.27s_Historic_centre_-_UNESCO_World_Heritage_centre_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cracow.27s_Historic_centre_-_UNESCO_World_Heritage_centre-77">[77]</a></sup> The <i>Stare Miasto</i> is the most prominent example of an old town in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-Gustafson_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gustafson-78">[78]</a></sup> For many centuries Kraków was <a href="/wiki/List_of_Polish_monarchs" title="List of Polish monarchs">the royal</a> capital of Poland, until <a href="/wiki/Sigismund_III_Vasa" title="Sigismund III Vasa">Sigismund III Vasa</a> relocated the court to <a href="/wiki/Warsaw" title="Warsaw">Warsaw</a> in 1596. The whole district is bisected by <a href="/wiki/Royal_Road,_Krak%C3%B3w" title="Royal Road, Kraków">the Royal Road</a>, the coronation route traversed by the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Polish_monarchs" title="List of Polish monarchs">Kings of Poland</a>. The Route begins at <a href="/wiki/St._Florian%27s_Church" title="St. Florian's Church">St. Florian's Church</a> outside the northern flank of the old city-walls in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">medieval</a> suburb of Kleparz; passes the <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w_barbican" class="mw-redirect" title="Kraków barbican">Barbican of Kraków</a> (<i>Barbakan</i>) built in 1499, and enters <i>Stare Miasto</i> through the <a href="/wiki/Florian_Gate" class="mw-redirect" title="Florian Gate">Florian Gate</a>. It leads down Floriańska Street through the Main Square, and up Grodzka to <a href="/wiki/Wawel" title="Wawel">Wawel</a>, the former seat of Polish royalty, overlooking the <a href="/wiki/Vistula_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Vistula River">Vistula river</a>. Old Town attracts visitors from all over the World. Kraków historic centre is one of the 13 places in Poland that are included in the UNESCO <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Sites</a>. The architectural design of the district had survived all cataclysms of the past and retained its original form coming from the medieval times. The Old Town of Kraków is home to about six thousand historic sites and more than two million works of art.<sup id="cite_ref-architecture72_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-architecture72-79">[79]</a></sup> Its rich variety of heritage architecture includes <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_medieval_Poland" title="Culture of medieval Poland">Gothic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_in_Poland" title="Renaissance in Poland">Renaissance</a> and <a href="/wiki/Baroque_in_Poland" title="Baroque in Poland">Baroque</a> buildings. Kraków's palaces, churches, theatres and mansions display great variety of color, architectural details, <a href="/wiki/Stained_glass" title="Stained glass">stained glass</a>, paintings, sculptures, and furnishings.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Krakow_Kanonicza_20070804_1000.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Krakow_Kanonicza_20070804_1000.jpg/220px-Krakow_Kanonicza_20070804_1000.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Krakow_Kanonicza_20070804_1000.jpg/330px-Krakow_Kanonicza_20070804_1000.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Krakow_Kanonicza_20070804_1000.jpg/440px-Krakow_Kanonicza_20070804_1000.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2256" data-file-height="1500" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Krakow_Kanonicza_20070804_1000.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Kanonicza Street, at the foot of the <a href="/wiki/Wawel_Castle" title="Wawel Castle">Wawel Castle</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In addition to the old town, the city's district of <a href="/wiki/Kazimierz" title="Kazimierz">Kazimierz</a> is particularly notable for its many renaissance buildings and picturesque streets, as well as the historic Jewish quarter located in the north-eastern part of Kazimierz. Kazimierz was founded in the 14th century to the south-east of the city centre and soon became a wealthy, well-populated area where construction of imposing properties became commonplace. Perhaps the most important feature of medieval Kazimierz was the only major, permanent bridge (<i>Pons Regalis</i>) across the northern arm of the Vistula. This natural barrier used to separate Kazimierz from the Old Town for several centuries, while the bridge connected Kraków to the <a href="/wiki/Wieliczka_Salt_Mine" title="Wieliczka Salt Mine">Wieliczka Salt Mine</a> and the lucrative Hungarian trade route. The last structure at this location (at the end of modern Stradom Street) was dismantled in 1880 when the northern arm of the river was filled in with earth and rock, and subsequently built over.<sup id="cite_ref-.C5.9Awiszczowski_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-.C5.9Awiszczowski-28">[28]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wandaluzja-1_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wandaluzja-1-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:442px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Krak%C3%B3w_239a.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Krak%C3%B3w_239a.jpg/440px-Krak%C3%B3w_239a.jpg" width="440" height="169" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Krak%C3%B3w_239a.jpg/660px-Krak%C3%B3w_239a.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Krak%C3%B3w_239a.jpg/880px-Krak%C3%B3w_239a.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4324" data-file-height="1657" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Krak%C3%B3w_239a.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
View of Kraków from St. Mary's Basilica in the Market Square</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>By the 1930s, Kraków had 120 officially <a href="/wiki/Synagogues_of_Krak%C3%B3w" title="Synagogues of Kraków">registered synagogues</a> and prayer houses that spanned across the old city. Much of Jewish intellectual life had moved to new centres like <a href="/wiki/Podg%C3%B3rze" title="Podgórze">Podgórze</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-krakow.jewish.org.pl-pdf_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-krakow.jewish.org.pl-pdf-81">[81]</a></sup> This in turn, led to the redevelopment and renovation of much of Kazimierz and the development of new districts in Kraków. Most historic buildings in central Kazimierz today are preserved in their original form. Some old buildings however, were not repaired after the devastation brought by the Second World War, and have remained empty. Most recent efforts at restoring the historic neighborhoods gained new impetus around 1993. Kazimierz is now a well-visited area, seeing a booming growth in Jewish-themed restaurants, bars, bookstores and souvenir shops.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:DZolopa_033_2013.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/DZolopa_033_2013.jpg/220px-DZolopa_033_2013.jpg" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/DZolopa_033_2013.jpg/330px-DZolopa_033_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/DZolopa_033_2013.jpg/440px-DZolopa_033_2013.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3817" data-file-height="2491" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:DZolopa_033_2013.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w_Society_of_Friends_of_Fine_Arts" title="Kraków Society of Friends of Fine Arts">Palace of Art</a> at Szczepański Square, is an example of <a href="/wiki/Art_Nouveau" title="Art Nouveau">Art Nouveau</a> architecture in central Kraków <sup id="cite_ref-Palace_of_Art_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Palace_of_Art-82">[82]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As the city of Kraków began to expand further under the rule of the <a href="/wiki/Austro-Hungarian_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Austro-Hungarian Empire">Austro-Hungarian Empire</a>, the new architectural styles also developed. Key buildings from the 19th and early 20th centuries in Kraków include the Jan Matejko Academy of Fine Arts, the directorate of the Polish State Railways as well as the original complex of <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w_G%C5%82%C3%B3wny_railway_station" title="Kraków Główny railway station">Kraków Główny railway station</a> and the city's <a href="/wiki/Cracow_University_of_Economics" class="mw-redirect" title="Cracow University of Economics">Academy of Economics</a>. It was also at around that time that Kraków's first radial boulevards began to appear, with the city undergoing a large-scale program aimed at transforming the ancient Polish capital into a sophisticated regional centre of the Austro-Hungarian Empire. New representative government buildings and multi-story tenement houses were built at around that time. Much of the urban-planning beyond the walls of the Old Town was done by Polish architects and engineers trained in <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>. Some major projects of the era include the development of the <a href="/wiki/Jagiellonian_University" title="Jagiellonian University">Jagiellonian University</a>'s new premises and the building of the <a href="/wiki/Collegium_Novum" title="Collegium Novum">Collegium Novum</a> just west of the Old Town. The imperial style planning of the city's further development continued until the return of Poland's independence, following the First World War. Early modernist style in Kraków is represented by such masterpieces as <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w_Society_of_Friends_of_Fine_Arts" title="Kraków Society of Friends of Fine Arts">the Palace of Art</a> by <a href="/wiki/Franciszek_M%C4%85czy%C5%84ski" title="Franciszek Mączyński">Franciszek Mączyński</a> and the 'House under the Globe'. <a href="/wiki/Vienna_Secession#Architecture" title="Vienna Secession">Secession style</a> architecture, which had arrived in Kraków from <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>, became popular towards the end of <a href="/wiki/Partitions_of_Poland" title="Partitions of Poland">the Partitions</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Strasz_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Strasz-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Basztowa_Ur.Woj_i_NBP,_Krakow.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Basztowa_Ur.Woj_i_NBP%2C_Krakow.jpg/170px-Basztowa_Ur.Woj_i_NBP%2C_Krakow.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Basztowa_Ur.Woj_i_NBP%2C_Krakow.jpg/255px-Basztowa_Ur.Woj_i_NBP%2C_Krakow.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Basztowa_Ur.Woj_i_NBP%2C_Krakow.jpg/340px-Basztowa_Ur.Woj_i_NBP%2C_Krakow.jpg 2x" data-file-width="835" data-file-height="1115" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Basztowa_Ur.Woj_i_NBP,_Krakow.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Basztowa Street</i>, filled with some of the most unique historical buildings in all architectural styles; part of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Road,_Krak%C3%B3w" title="Royal Road, Kraków">Royal Route of Kraków</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>With Poland's regained independence came the major change in the fortunes of Kraków—now the second most important city of a sovereign nation. The state began to make new plans for the city development and commissioned a number of representative buildings. The predominant style for new projects was modernism with various interpretations of the art-deco style.<sup id="cite_ref-Vogt-Nassery_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vogt-Nassery-84">[84]</a></sup> Important buildings constructed in the style of <a href="/wiki/Polish_modernism" class="mw-redirect" title="Polish modernism">Polish modernism</a> include the Feniks 'LOT' building on Basztowa Street, the Feniks department store on the <a href="/wiki/Main_Market_Square,_Krak%C3%B3w" class="mw-redirect" title="Main Market Square, Kraków">Main Square</a> and the Municipal Savings Bank on Szczepański Square. The Józef Piłsudski house is also of note as a particularly good example of interwar architecture in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-Krak.C3.B3w.2C_Oleandry_.E2.80.93_Dom_im._J.C3.B3zefa_Pi.C5.82sudskiego_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Krak.C3.B3w.2C_Oleandry_.E2.80.93_Dom_im._J.C3.B3zefa_Pi.C5.82sudskiego-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the Second World War, new government turned toward Soviet influence and the <a href="/wiki/Stalinist_architecture" title="Stalinist architecture">Stalinist monumentalism</a>. The doctrine of <a href="/wiki/Socialist_realism_in_Poland" title="Socialist realism in Poland">Socialist realism in Poland</a>, as in other countries of the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic" title="People's Republic">People's Republics</a>, was enforced from 1949 to 1956. It involved all domains of art, but its most spectacular achievements were made in the field of urban design. The guidelines for this new trend were spelled-out in a 1949 resolution of the National Council of Party Architects. Architecture was to become a weapon in establishing the new social order by the communists.<sup id="cite_ref-inyourpocket.2Fsightseeing_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inyourpocket.2Fsightseeing-86">[86]</a></sup> The ideological impact of urban design was valued more than aesthetics. It aimed at expressing persistence and power. This form of architecture was implemented in the new industrial district of Nowa Huta with apartment blocks constructed according to a Stalinist blueprint, with repetitious courtyards and wide, tree-lined avenues.<sup id="cite_ref-Nh.pl-1_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nh.pl-1-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pawilon_Wyspia%C5%84ski_2000,_Krak%C3%B3w.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Pawilon_Wyspia%C5%84ski_2000%2C_Krak%C3%B3w.JPG/220px-Pawilon_Wyspia%C5%84ski_2000%2C_Krak%C3%B3w.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Pawilon_Wyspia%C5%84ski_2000%2C_Krak%C3%B3w.JPG/330px-Pawilon_Wyspia%C5%84ski_2000%2C_Krak%C3%B3w.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Pawilon_Wyspia%C5%84ski_2000%2C_Krak%C3%B3w.JPG/440px-Pawilon_Wyspia%C5%84ski_2000%2C_Krak%C3%B3w.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pawilon_Wyspia%C5%84ski_2000,_Krak%C3%B3w.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Pawilon Wyspiański 2000 is a rare piece of <a href="/wiki/Postmodern_architecture" title="Postmodern architecture">Postmodern architecture</a> present in Krakow's <i>Old Town</i><sup id="cite_ref-sztuka-architektury1_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sztuka-architektury1-88">[88]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Since the style of the <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_in_Poland" title="Renaissance in Poland">Renaissance</a> was generally regarded as the most revered in old Polish architecture, it was also used for augmenting Poland's <a href="/wiki/Socialist_realism_in_Poland" title="Socialist realism in Poland">Socialist national</a> format. However, in the course of incorporating the principles of Socialist realism, there were quite a few deviations introduced by the communists. One of these was to more closely reflect Soviet architecture, which resulted in the majority of works blending into one another. From 1953, critical opinions in the Party were increasingly frequent, and the doctrine was given up in 1956 marking the end of <a href="/wiki/Stalinism_in_Poland" class="mw-redirect" title="Stalinism in Poland">Stalinism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SOCREALIZM_in_Poland_.281949.E2.80.931955.29_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SOCREALIZM_in_Poland_.281949.E2.80.931955.29-89">[89]</a></sup> Currently the <a href="/wiki/Socrealism" class="mw-redirect" title="Socrealism">soc-realist</a> centre of Nowa Huta is considered to be a meritorious monument of the times. This period in postwar architecture was followed by the mass-construction of large <a href="/wiki/Plattenbau" title="Plattenbau">Panel System</a> apartment blocks, most of which were built outside the city centre and thus do not encroach upon the beauty of the old or new towns. Some examples of the new style (e.g., Hotel Cracovia) recently listed as heritage monuments were built during the later half of the 20th century in Kraków.<sup id="cite_ref-naszemiasto-cracovia_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-naszemiasto-cracovia-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/Revolutions_of_1989" title="Revolutions of 1989">Revolutions of 1989</a> and the birth of the <a href="/wiki/Third_Polish_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Third Polish Republic">Third Republic</a> in the later half of the 20th century, a number of new architectural projects were completed, including the construction of large business parks and commercial facilities such as the <a href="/wiki/Galeria_Krakowska" title="Galeria Krakowska">Galeria Krakowska</a>, or infrastructure investments like the <a href="/wiki/Tramways_in_Krak%C3%B3w#Krak.C3.B3w_Fast_Tram" class="mw-redirect" title="Tramways in Kraków">Kraków Fast Tram</a>, giving the city a great deal of quality solutions blending with its centuries-old heritage. A good example of this would be the 2007-built <i>Pawilon Wyspiański 2000</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-sztuka-architektury1_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sztuka-architektury1-88">[88]</a></sup> which is used as a multi-purpose information and exhibition space, or the award-winning Małopolski Garden of Arts (<i><a href="https://pl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ma%C5%82opolski_Ogr%C3%B3d_Sztuki_w_Krakowie" class="extiw" title="pl:Małopolski Ogród Sztuki w Krakowie">Małopolski Ogród Sztuki</a></i>), a multi-purpose exhibition and theatre complex located in the historic Old Town.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parks_and_gardens">Parks and gardens</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Krak%C3%B3w&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Parks and gardens">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:006Planty.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/006Planty.JPG/220px-006Planty.JPG" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/006Planty.JPG/330px-006Planty.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/006Planty.JPG/440px-006Planty.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1360" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:006Planty.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Fountain in the <a href="/wiki/Planty_Park" title="Planty Park">Planty Park</a>, which surrounds Kraków's <i>Old Town</i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>There are about 40 parks in Kraków including dozens of gardens and forests.<sup id="cite_ref-wse.krakow_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wse.krakow-92">[92]</a></sup> Several, like the <a href="/wiki/Planty_Park" title="Planty Park">Planty Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Botanical_Garden_in_Krak%C3%B3w" class="mw-redirect" title="Botanical Garden in Kraków">Botanical Garden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Park_Krakowski" title="Park Krakowski">Park Krakowski</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jordan_Park" title="Jordan Park">Jordan Park</a> and <a href="/wiki/B%C5%82onia_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="Błonia Park">Błonia Park</a> are located in the centre of the city; with Zakrzówek, Lasek Wolski forest, Strzelecki Park and Park Lotników (among others) in the surrounding districts.<sup id="cite_ref-wse.krakow_92-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wse.krakow-92">[92]</a></sup> Parks cover about 318.5 hectares (2002) of the city.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Planty_Park" title="Planty Park">Planty Park</a> is the best-known park in Kraków. It was established between 1822 and 1830 in place of the old city walls, forming a <a href="/wiki/Green_belt" title="Green belt">green belt</a> around the Old Town. It consists of a chain of smaller gardens designed in various styles and adorned with monuments. The park has an area of 21 hectares (52 acres) and a length of 4 kilometres (2.5&#160;mi), forming a scenic walkway popular with Cracovians.<sup id="cite_ref-Strzala1_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Strzala1-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Jordan_Park" title="Jordan Park">Jordan Park</a> founded in 1889 by Dr <a href="/wiki/Henryk_Jordan" title="Henryk Jordan">Henryk Jordan</a>, was the first public park of its kind in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-grodzka.net_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grodzka.net-94">[94]</a></sup> The park built on the banks of the <a href="/wiki/Rudawa_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Rudawa River">Rudawa river</a> was equipped with running and exercise tracks, playgrounds, the swimming pool, <a href="/wiki/Amphitheatre" title="Amphitheatre">amphitheatre</a>, pavilions, and a pond for <a href="/wiki/Watercraft_rowing" class="mw-redirect" title="Watercraft rowing">boat rowing</a> and water bicycles. It is located on the grounds of a larger Kraków’s <a href="/wiki/B%C5%82onia_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="Błonia Park">Błonia Park</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-History.2C_philosophy_and_photographs_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History.2C_philosophy_and_photographs-95">[95]</a></sup> The less prominent <a href="/wiki/Park_Krakowski" title="Park Krakowski">Park Krakowski</a> was founded in 1885 by <a href="/wiki/Stanis%C5%82aw_Rehman" title="Stanisław Rehman">Stanisław Rehman</a> but has since been greatly reduced in size because of rapid <a href="/wiki/Real_estate_development" title="Real estate development">real estate development</a>. It was a popular destination point with many Cracovians at the end of the 19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-encyklopedia3_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-encyklopedia3-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environment">Environment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Krak%C3%B3w&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Environment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There are five <a href="/wiki/Protected_areas_of_Poland" title="Protected areas of Poland">nature reserves</a> in Kraków with a total area of 48.6 ha.<sup id="cite_ref-gdos_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gdos-97">[97]</a></sup> Smaller green zones constitute parts of the <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w-Cz%C4%99stochowa_Upland" title="Kraków-Częstochowa Upland">Kraków-Częstochowa Upland</a> Jurassic Landscape Parks' Board, which deals with the protection areas of the Polish Jura. Under its jurisdiction are: the <a href="/wiki/Bielany-Tyniec_Landscape_Park" title="Bielany-Tyniec Landscape Park">Bielany-Tyniec Landscape Park</a> (Park Bielańsko-Tyniecki), <a href="/wiki/Tenczynek_Landscape_Park" title="Tenczynek Landscape Park">Tenczynek Landscape Park</a> (Park Tencziński) and <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w_Valleys_Landscape_Park" title="Kraków Valleys Landscape Park">Kraków Valleys Landscape Park</a> (Park Krajobrazowy Dolinki Krakowskie), with their watersheds. All natural reserves of the Polish Jura Chain are part of the <a href="/wiki/CORINE" class="mw-redirect" title="CORINE">CORINE</a> biotopes programme due to their unique flora, fauna, geomorphology and landscape. The western part of Kraków constitute the so-called Obszar Krakowski ecological network, including the ecological corridor of the Vistula river. The southern slopes of limestone hills provide conditions for the development of <a href="/wiki/Thermophile" title="Thermophile">thermophilous</a> vegetation, grasslands and <a href="/wiki/Shrubland" title="Shrubland">scrubs</a>.</p>
<p>The city is spaced along an extended latitudinal transect of the <a href="/wiki/Vistula" title="Vistula">Vistula</a> River Valley with a network of tributaries including its right tributary Wilga, and left: <a href="/wiki/Rudawa_(river)" title="Rudawa (river)">Rudawa</a>, Białucha, <a href="/wiki/D%C5%82ubnia" class="mw-redirect" title="Dłubnia">Dłubnia</a> and Sanka. The rivers and their valleys along with bodies of water are some of the most interesting natural wonders of Kraków.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Krak%C3%B3w&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For more details on this topic, see <a href="/wiki/Local_government_in_Krak%C3%B3w" title="Local government in Kraków">Local government in Kraków</a>.</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jacek_Majchrowski.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Jacek_Majchrowski.JPG/170px-Jacek_Majchrowski.JPG" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Jacek_Majchrowski.JPG/255px-Jacek_Majchrowski.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Jacek_Majchrowski.JPG/340px-Jacek_Majchrowski.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1224" data-file-height="1836" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jacek_Majchrowski.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
President of Kraków, <a href="/wiki/Jacek_Majchrowski" title="Jacek Majchrowski">Jacek Majchrowski</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Kraków City Council has 43 elected members,<sup id="cite_ref-Radni_Miasta_Krakowa_V_kadencji_.28.27.27Krak.C3.B3w_City_Councillors_of_the_5th_term.27.27.29_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Radni_Miasta_Krakowa_V_kadencji_.28.27.27Krak.C3.B3w_City_Councillors_of_the_5th_term.27.27.29-98">[98]</a></sup> one of whom is the mayor, or President of Kraków, elected every four years. The election of the City Council and of the local <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-BPI_113_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BPI_113-99">[99]</a></sup> which takes place at the same time, is based on legislation introduced on 20 June 2002. The current President of Kraków, re-elected for his fourth term in 2014, is <a href="/wiki/Jacek_Majchrowski" title="Jacek Majchrowski">Jacek Majchrowski</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Municipality.2C_Mayor_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Municipality.2C_Mayor-100">[100]</a></sup> Several members of the Polish national Parliament (<a href="/wiki/Sejm" title="Sejm">Sejm</a>) are elected from the <a href="/wiki/Members_of_Polish_Sejm_elected_from_Krak%C3%B3w_constituency" title="Members of Polish Sejm elected from Kraków constituency">Kraków constituency</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Members_of_Polish_Sejm_elected_from_Krak.C3.B3w_constituency_-_VisWiki_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Members_of_Polish_Sejm_elected_from_Krak.C3.B3w_constituency_-_VisWiki-101">[101]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Symbols_of_Krak%C3%B3w" title="Symbols of Kraków">city's official symbols</a> include a <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms" title="Coat of arms">coat of arms</a>, a flag, a seal, and a banner.<sup id="cite_ref-ordinance_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ordinance-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pa%C5%82ac_Wielopolskich_w_Krakowie,_2011.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Pa%C5%82ac_Wielopolskich_w_Krakowie%2C_2011.jpg/220px-Pa%C5%82ac_Wielopolskich_w_Krakowie%2C_2011.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Pa%C5%82ac_Wielopolskich_w_Krakowie%2C_2011.jpg/330px-Pa%C5%82ac_Wielopolskich_w_Krakowie%2C_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Pa%C5%82ac_Wielopolskich_w_Krakowie%2C_2011.jpg/440px-Pa%C5%82ac_Wielopolskich_w_Krakowie%2C_2011.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1915" data-file-height="1438" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pa%C5%82ac_Wielopolskich_w_Krakowie,_2011.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Wielopolski_Palace" title="Wielopolski Palace">Wielopolski Palace</a> (1560), the seat of Kraków's mayor, administration and city council</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The responsibilities of Kraków's president include drafting and implementing resolutions, enacting city bylaws, managing the city budget, employing city administrators, and preparing against floods and <a href="/wiki/Natural_disaster" title="Natural disaster">natural disasters</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BPI_113_99-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BPI_113-99">[99]</a></sup> The president fulfills his duties with the help of the City Council, city managers and city inspectors. In the 1990s, the <a href="/wiki/Local_government" title="Local government">city government</a> was reorganised to better differentiate between its <a href="/wiki/Political_agenda" title="Political agenda">political agenda</a> and administrative functions. As a result, the Office of Public Information was created to handle inquiries and foster communication between city departments and citizens at large.<sup id="cite_ref-Institutional_Capital:_Building_Post-communist_Government_Performance_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Institutional_Capital:_Building_Post-communist_Government_Performance-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2000, the city government introduced a new long-term program called "Safer City" in cooperation with the Police, Traffic, Social Services, Fire, <a href="/wiki/Public_Safety" class="mw-redirect" title="Public Safety">Public Safety</a>, and the Youth Departments. Subsequently, the number of criminal offences went down by 3 percent between 2000 and 2001, and the rate of detection increased by 1.4 percent to a total of 30.2 percent in the same period.<sup id="cite_ref-krakow_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-krakow-104">[104]</a></sup> The city is receiving help in carrying out the program from all educational institutions and the local media, including TV, radio and the press.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Districts">Districts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Krak%C3%B3w&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Districts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Krak%C3%B3w" title="Districts of Kraków">Districts of Kraków</a></div>
<p>Kraków is divided into 18 administrative districts (<i><a href="/wiki/Dzielnica" title="Dzielnica">dzielnica</a></i>) or boroughs, each with a degree of autonomy within its own municipal government.<sup id="cite_ref-districts_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-districts-105">[105]</a></sup> Prior to March 1991, the city had been divided into four quarters which still give a sense of identity to Kraków – the towns of <a href="/wiki/Podg%C3%B3rze" title="Podgórze">Podgórze</a>, Nowa Huta, and <a href="/wiki/Krowodrza" title="Krowodrza">Krowodrza</a> which were amalgamated into the city of Kraków as it expanded, and the ancient town centre of Kraków itself.<sup id="cite_ref-districts_105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-districts-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Krak%C3%B3w,_Pomnik_Grunwaldzki_-_fotopolska.eu_(331528).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Krak%C3%B3w%2C_Pomnik_Grunwaldzki_-_fotopolska.eu_%28331528%29.jpg/170px-Krak%C3%B3w%2C_Pomnik_Grunwaldzki_-_fotopolska.eu_%28331528%29.jpg" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Krak%C3%B3w%2C_Pomnik_Grunwaldzki_-_fotopolska.eu_%28331528%29.jpg/255px-Krak%C3%B3w%2C_Pomnik_Grunwaldzki_-_fotopolska.eu_%28331528%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Krak%C3%B3w%2C_Pomnik_Grunwaldzki_-_fotopolska.eu_%28331528%29.jpg/340px-Krak%C3%B3w%2C_Pomnik_Grunwaldzki_-_fotopolska.eu_%28331528%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="833" data-file-height="1250" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Krak%C3%B3w,_Pomnik_Grunwaldzki_-_fotopolska.eu_(331528).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Matejko Square at <a href="/wiki/Kleparz" title="Kleparz">Kleparz</a> is one of the city's most important public spaces</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The oldest neighborhoods of Kraków were incorporated into the city before the late-18th century. They include the Old Town (<i><a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w_Old_Town" title="Kraków Old Town">Stare Miasto</a></i>), once contained within the <a href="/wiki/Florian_Gate" class="mw-redirect" title="Florian Gate">city defensive walls</a> and now encircled by the Planty park; the <a href="/wiki/Wawel" title="Wawel">Wawel</a> District, which is the site of the Royal Castle and the cathedral; Stradom and Kazimierz, the latter originally divided into Christian and Jewish quarters;<sup id="cite_ref-Krakow.2C_Auschwitz_and_Warsaw_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Krakow.2C_Auschwitz_and_Warsaw-106">[106]</a></sup> as well as the ancient town of <a href="/wiki/Kleparz" title="Kleparz">Kleparz</a>.</p>
<p>Major districts added in the 19th and 20th centuries include <a href="/wiki/Podg%C3%B3rze" title="Podgórze">Podgórze</a>, which until 1915, was a separate town on the southern bank of the Vistula, and Nowa Huta, east of the city centre, built after World War II.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nowa_Huta_jako_idealne_socjalistyczne_miasto.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Nowa_Huta_jako_idealne_socjalistyczne_miasto.jpg/220px-Nowa_Huta_jako_idealne_socjalistyczne_miasto.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Nowa_Huta_jako_idealne_socjalistyczne_miasto.jpg/330px-Nowa_Huta_jako_idealne_socjalistyczne_miasto.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Nowa_Huta_jako_idealne_socjalistyczne_miasto.jpg/440px-Nowa_Huta_jako_idealne_socjalistyczne_miasto.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4096" data-file-height="2732" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nowa_Huta_jako_idealne_socjalistyczne_miasto.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Socialist_realism_in_Poland" title="Socialist realism in Poland">Socialist-realist</a> district of <a href="/wiki/Nowa_Huta" title="Nowa Huta">Nowa Huta</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Among the most notable historic districts of the city are: <a href="/wiki/Wawel_Hill" class="mw-redirect" title="Wawel Hill">Wawel Hill</a>, home to <a href="/wiki/Wawel_Castle" title="Wawel Castle">Wawel Castle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wawel_Cathedral" title="Wawel Cathedral">Wawel Cathedral</a>, where many historic Polish kings are buried; the medieval Old Town, with its <a href="/wiki/Main_Market_Square,_Krak%C3%B3w" class="mw-redirect" title="Main Market Square, Kraków">Main Market Square</a> (200 metres (660&#160;ft) square); dozens of old churches and museums; the 14th-century buildings of the Jagiellonian University; and Kazimierz, the historical centre of Kraków's Jewish social and religious life.<sup id="cite_ref-Krakow_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Krakow-107">[107]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Old Town district of Kraków is home to about 6,000 historic sites, and more than 2,000,000 works of art.<sup id="cite_ref-architecture72_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-architecture72-79">[79]</a></sup> Its rich variety of historic architecture includes <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_architecture" title="Renaissance architecture">Renaissance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baroque_architecture" title="Baroque architecture">Baroque</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gothic_architecture" title="Gothic architecture">Gothic</a> buildings. Kraków's palaces, churches and mansions display great variety of colour, architectural details, <a href="/wiki/Stained_glass" title="Stained glass">stained glass</a>, paintings, sculptures, and furnishings.</p>
<p>In the Market Square stands the Gothic <a href="/wiki/St._Mary%27s_Basilica,_Krak%C3%B3w" title="St. Mary's Basilica, Kraków">St. Mary's Basilica</a> (<i>Kościół Mariacki</i>). It was rebuilt in the 14th-century and features the famous wooden altar (<a href="/wiki/Altarpiece_of_Veit_Stoss" class="mw-redirect" title="Altarpiece of Veit Stoss">Altarpiece of Veit Stoss</a>), the largest Gothic altarpiece in the world,<sup id="cite_ref-Kurtz_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kurtz-108">[108]</a></sup> carved by <a href="/wiki/Veit_Stoss" title="Veit Stoss">Veit Stoss</a>. From the church's main tower a trumpet call (<i><a href="/wiki/Hejna%C5%82_mariacki" class="mw-redirect" title="Hejnał mariacki">hejnał mariacki</a></i>), is sounded every hour. The melody, which used to announce the opening and closing of city gates, ends unexpectedly in midstream. According to legend, the tune was played during the 13th-century <a href="/wiki/Tatars" title="Tatars">Tatar</a> invasion by a guard warning citizens against the attack. He was shot by an archer of the invading Tatar forces whilst playing, the bugle call breaking off at the moment he died.<sup id="cite_ref-hejnal_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hejnal-109">[109]</a></sup> The story was recounted in a book published in the late-1920s called <i><a href="/wiki/The_Trumpeter_of_Krakow" title="The Trumpeter of Krakow">The Trumpeter of Krakow</a></i>, by <a href="/wiki/Eric_P._Kelly" title="Eric P. Kelly">Eric P. Kelly</a>, which won a <a href="/wiki/Newbery_Medal" title="Newbery Medal">Newbery Award</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-JPKelly_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JPKelly-110">[110]</a></sup></p>

</table>
<p>The current divisions were introduced by the Kraków City Hall on 19 April 1995. Districts were assigned <a href="/wiki/Roman_numerals" title="Roman numerals">Roman numerals</a> as well as the current name:<sup id="cite_ref-krakow1_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-krakow1-112">[112]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w_Old_Town" title="Kraków Old Town">Stare Miasto</a> (I), <a href="/wiki/Grzeg%C3%B3rzki,_Krak%C3%B3w" class="mw-redirect" title="Grzegórzki, Kraków">Grzegórzki</a> (II), <a href="/wiki/Pr%C4%85dnik_Czerwony" title="Prądnik Czerwony">Prądnik Czerwony</a> (III), <a href="/wiki/Pr%C4%85dnik_Bia%C5%82y" title="Prądnik Biały">Prądnik Biały</a> (IV), <a href="/wiki/Krowodrza" title="Krowodrza">Łobzów</a> (V), <a href="/wiki/Bronowice,_Krak%C3%B3w" class="mw-redirect" title="Bronowice, Kraków">Bronowice</a> (VI), <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w-Zwierzyniec" class="mw-redirect" title="Kraków-Zwierzyniec">Zwierzyniec</a> (VII), <a href="/wiki/D%C4%99bniki,_Krak%C3%B3w" class="mw-redirect" title="Dębniki, Kraków">Dębniki</a> (VIII), <a href="/wiki/%C5%81agiewniki-Borek_Fa%C5%82%C4%99cki" title="Łagiewniki-Borek Fałęcki">Łagiewniki-Borek Fałęcki</a> (IX), <a href="/wiki/Swoszowice,_Krak%C3%B3w" class="mw-redirect" title="Swoszowice, Kraków">Swoszowice</a> (X), <a href="/wiki/Podg%C3%B3rze_Duchackie" title="Podgórze Duchackie">Podgórze Duchackie</a> (XI), <a href="/wiki/Bie%C5%BCan%C3%B3w-Prokocim" title="Bieżanów-Prokocim">Bieżanów-Prokocim</a> (XII), <a href="/wiki/Podg%C3%B3rze" title="Podgórze">Podgórze</a> (XIII), <a href="/wiki/Czy%C5%BCyny" title="Czyżyny">Czyżyny</a> (XIV), <a href="/wiki/Mistrzejowice" title="Mistrzejowice">Mistrzejowice</a> (XV), <a href="/wiki/Bie%C5%84czyce,_Krak%C3%B3w" class="mw-redirect" title="Bieńczyce, Kraków">Bieńczyce</a> (XVI), <a href="/wiki/Wzg%C3%B3rza_Krzes%C5%82awickie" title="Wzgórza Krzesławickie">Wzgórza Krzesławickie</a> (XVII), and <a href="/wiki/Nowa_Huta" title="Nowa Huta">Nowa Huta</a> (XVIII).</p>
<div style="clear:left;"></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Krak%C3%B3w&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Krakow-Cracovia_Business_Center.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Krakow-Cracovia_Business_Center.jpg/170px-Krakow-Cracovia_Business_Center.jpg" width="170" height="230" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Krakow-Cracovia_Business_Center.jpg/255px-Krakow-Cracovia_Business_Center.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Krakow-Cracovia_Business_Center.jpg/340px-Krakow-Cracovia_Business_Center.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="1383" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Krakow-Cracovia_Business_Center.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Cracovia</i> Business Centre</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Kraków is one of Poland's most important economic centres and the economic hub of the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Poland" title="Lesser Poland">Lesser Poland</a> (Małopolska) region.<sup id="cite_ref-gosp_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gosp-113">[113]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-krakplgosp_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-krakplgosp-114">[114]</a></sup> Since the fall of communism, the private sector has been growing steadily. There are about 50 large <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational companies</a> in the city, including <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a>, <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Dutch_Shell" title="Royal Dutch Shell">Royal Dutch Shell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Motorola" title="Motorola">Motorola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delphi" title="Delphi">Delphi</a>, <a href="/wiki/MAN_SE" title="MAN SE">MAN SE</a>, <a href="/wiki/General_Electric" title="General Electric">General Electric</a>, <a href="/wiki/ABB_Group" title="ABB Group">ABB</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aon_Hewitt" title="Aon Hewitt">Aon Hewitt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cisco_Systems" title="Cisco Systems">Cisco Systems</a> <a href="/wiki/Hitachi_Ltd." class="mw-redirect" title="Hitachi Ltd.">Hitachi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Altria_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Altria Group">Philip Morris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Capgemini" title="Capgemini">Capgemini</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-capgemini_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-capgemini-115">[115]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Sabre_Holdings" class="mw-redirect" title="Sabre Holdings">Sabre Holdings</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-About_Sabre_Holdings_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About_Sabre_Holdings-116">[116]</a></sup> along with other British, German and Scandinavian-based firms.<sup id="cite_ref-gosp_113-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gosp-113">[113]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pbs_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pbs-117">[117]</a></sup> The city is also the global headquarters for <a href="/wiki/Comarch" title="Comarch">Comarch</a>, a Polish enterprise software house. In 2005, <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">Foreign direct investment</a> in Kraków has reached approximately US$3,500,000,000. Kraków has been trying to model itself as a European version of Silicon Valley,<sup id="cite_ref-pbworks.com_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pbworks.com-118">[118]</a></sup> based on the large number of local and foreign hi-tech companies.<sup id="cite_ref-gosp_113-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gosp-113">[113]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Unemployment" title="Unemployment">unemployment rate</a> in Kraków was 4.8% in May 2007, well below the national average of 13%.<sup id="cite_ref-krakplgosp_114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-krakplgosp-114">[114]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Current_statistics_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Current_statistics-119">[119]</a></sup> Kraków is the second most-visited city in Poland (after <a href="/wiki/Warsaw" title="Warsaw">Warsaw</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-gosp_113-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gosp-113">[113]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-krakplgosp_114-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-krakplgosp-114">[114]</a></sup> According to the World Investment Report 2011 by the UN Conference for Trade and Development (UNCTAD), Kraków is also the most emergent city location for investment in global BPO projects (Business Process Outsourcing) in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-PAIiIZ_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PAIiIZ-120">[120]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Biurowiec_Newton.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Biurowiec_Newton.JPG/220px-Biurowiec_Newton.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Biurowiec_Newton.JPG/330px-Biurowiec_Newton.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Biurowiec_Newton.JPG/440px-Biurowiec_Newton.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1066" data-file-height="800" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Biurowiec_Newton.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>The Center for Business Innovation</i> office complex in Kraków</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2011, the <a href="/wiki/Budget_of_Krak%C3%B3w" class="mw-redirect" title="Budget of Kraków">city budget</a>, which is presented by the <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_Krak%C3%B3w" class="mw-redirect" title="Mayor of Kraków">Mayor of Kraków</a> on 15 November annually, has a projected revenue of 3,500,000,000 <a href="/wiki/Polish_z%C5%82oty" title="Polish złoty">złoty</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-krakow2_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-krakow2-121">[121]</a></sup> The primary sources of revenue were as follows: 14% from the municipal taxation on real estate properties and the use of <a href="/wiki/Amenity" title="Amenity">amenities</a>, 30% in transfers from the national <a href="/wiki/Budget" title="Budget">budget</a>, and 34% in state subsidies. Projected expenditures, totaling 3,520,000,000 złoty, included 21% in city development costs and 79% in city maintenance costs. Of the maintenance costs, as much as 39% were spent on education and childcare. The City of Kraków's development costs included; 41% toward construction of roads, transport, and communication (combined), and 25% for the city's infrastructure and environment.<sup id="cite_ref-Biuletyn_Statystyczny_Miasta_Krakowa_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Biuletyn_Statystyczny_Miasta_Krakowa-122">[122]</a></sup> The city has a high <a href="/wiki/Bond_credit_rating" title="Bond credit rating">bond credit rating</a>, and some 60% of the population is under the age of 45.<sup id="cite_ref-krakplgosp_114-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-krakplgosp-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Knowledge_and_Innovation_Community_EIT">Knowledge and Innovation Community EIT</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Krak%C3%B3w&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Knowledge and Innovation Community EIT">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Kraków is one of the co-location centres of Knowledge and Innovation Community (Sustainable Energy) of The <a href="/wiki/European_Institute_of_Innovation_and_Technology" title="European Institute of Innovation and Technology">European Institute of Innovation and Technology</a> (EIT).<sup id="cite_ref-Knowledge_and_Innovation_Community_EIT.2C_at_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Knowledge_and_Innovation_Community_EIT.2C_at-123">[123]</a></sup></p>
<p>InnoEnergy is an integrated alliance of reputable organisations from the education, research and industry sectors. It was created based on long standing links of cooperation as well as the principles of excellence. The partners have jointly developed a strategy to tackle the weaknesses of the European innovation landscape in the field of sustainable energy.<sup id="cite_ref-europa_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-europa-124">[124]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Krak%C3%B3w&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Krak%C3%B3w" title="Transport in Kraków">Transport in Kraków</a></div>
<p>Public transport is based on a fairly dense network of tram and bus routes operated by a municipal company, supplemented by a number of private minibus operators. Local trains connect some of the suburbs. The bulk of the city's historic area has been turned into a <a href="/wiki/Pedestrian_zone" title="Pedestrian zone">pedestrian zone</a> with rickshaws and horse-drawn carriages; however, the tramlines run within a three-block radius <i>(pictured)</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Krakow._Varied_Means_of_Transportation_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Krakow._Varied_Means_of_Transportation-125">[125]</a></sup> The historic means of transportation in the city can be examined at the <a href="/wiki/Muzeum_In%C5%BCynierii_Miejskiej_w_Krakowie" title="Muzeum Inżynierii Miejskiej w Krakowie">Museum of Municipal Engineering</a> in the Kazimierz district, with many old trams, cars and buses.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup></p>
<p>Railway connections are available to most <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_and_towns_in_Poland" title="List of cities and towns in Poland">Polish cities</a>, e.g. <a href="/wiki/Katowice" title="Katowice">Katowice</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cz%C4%99stochowa" title="Częstochowa">Częstochowa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Szczecin" title="Szczecin">Szczecin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gdynia" title="Gdynia">Gdynia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Warsaw" title="Warsaw">Warsaw</a>. International destinations include <a href="/wiki/Bratislava" title="Bratislava">Bratislava</a>, <a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">Budapest</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">Prague</a>, <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lviv" title="Lviv">Lviv</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kiev" title="Kiev">Kiev</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Odessa" title="Odessa">Odessa</a> (June–September).<sup id="cite_ref-International_railway_connections_from_Krak.C3.B3w_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-International_railway_connections_from_Krak.C3.B3w-127">[127]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Krak%C3%B3w#Krak.C3.B3w_Central_station" title="Transport in Kraków">main railway station</a> is located just outside the Old Town District and is well-served by public transport.</p>
<p>Kraków's airport, officially named: <a href="/wiki/John_Paul_II_International_Airport_Krak%C3%B3w%E2%80%93Balice" title="John Paul II International Airport Kraków–Balice">John Paul II International Airport Kraków–Balice</a> (<a href="/wiki/International_Air_Transport_Association_airport_code" class="mw-redirect" title="International Air Transport Association airport code">IATA</a>: <b>KRK</b>), is located 11&#160;km (7&#160;mi) west of the city. Direct trains cover the route between <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w_G%C5%82%C3%B3wny" class="mw-redirect" title="Kraków Główny">Kraków Główny train station</a> and the airport in 20 minutes. Krakow Airport served around 5,000,000 passengers in 2016. Also, the <a href="/wiki/Katowice_International_Airport" title="Katowice International Airport">Katowice International Airport</a> is located 80 kilometres (50 miles) or about 75 minutes from Kraków.<sup id="cite_ref-e-krakow_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-e-krakow-128">[128]</a></sup></p>

<p>In Autumn 2016 Poland's oldest <a href="/wiki/Bicycle-sharing_system" title="Bicycle-sharing system">Bicycle-sharing system</a> was modernized and now offers 1500 bikes at 150 stations under the name of Wavelo.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Krak%C3%B3w&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Poland#Largest_metropolitan_and_urban_areas" title="Demographics of Poland">Urban demographics of Poland</a></div>
<p>Kraków had a recorded population of 762,508 in 2015. According to the 2006 data,<sup id="cite_ref-Census_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census-129">[129]</a></sup> the population of Kraków comprised about 2% of the population of Poland and 23% of the population of the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Poland_Voivodeship" title="Lesser Poland Voivodeship">Lesser Poland Voivodeship</a>. Selected demographic indicators are presented in a table (below), compiled on the basis of only the population living in Kraków permanently. The larger metropolitan area of the city encompasses a territory in which (in 2010) 1,393,893 inhabitants live.<sup id="cite_ref-stat_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stat-130">[130]</a></sup></p>
<p>Already in the Middle Ages, the population of Kraków consisting of numerous ethnic groups, began to grow rapidly.<sup id="cite_ref-Kras_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kras-131">[131]</a></sup> It doubled between 1100 and 1300 from 5,000 to 10,000, and in 1400 counted 14,000 inhabitants. By 1550, the population of metropolitan Kraków was 18,000; although it went down to 15,000 in the next fifty years due to calamity.<sup id="cite_ref-Keene_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Keene-132">[132]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sedlar_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sedlar-133">[133]</a></sup> By the early 17th century the Kraków population had reached 28,000 inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-Labno_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Labno-134">[134]</a></sup></p>
