<p>In the historical 1931 census preceding World War II, 78.1% of Cracovians declared Polish as their primary language, with Yiddish or Hebrew at 20.9%, Ukrainian 0.4%, German 0.3%, and Russian 0.1%.<sup id="cite_ref-encyklopedia_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-encyklopedia-135">[135]</a></sup> The ravages of history have greatly reduced the percentage of <a href="/wiki/Minority_group" title="Minority group">ethnic minorities</a> living in Kraków. The official and unofficial numbers differ, as in the case of <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">Romani people</a>. Hence, according to the 2002 census,<sup id="cite_ref-stat2_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stat2-136">[136]</a></sup> among those who have declared their national identity (irrespective of language and religion) in Kraków Voivodeship, 1,572 were <a href="/wiki/Slovaks" title="Slovaks">Slovaks</a>, followed by <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians" title="Ukrainians">Ukrainians</a> (472), Jews (50) and <a href="/wiki/Armenians" title="Armenians">Armenians</a> (22). <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">Romani people</a>, officially numbered at 1,678, are estimated at over 5,000. Statistics collected by the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_National_Education_of_the_Republic_of_Poland" class="mw-redirect" title="Ministry of National Education of the Republic of Poland">Ministry of Education</a> reveal that, even though only 1% of adults (<i>as per above</i>) officially claim minority status, as many as 3% of students participate in programmes designed for ethnic minorities.<sup id="cite_ref-Raport_z_realizacji_priorytetowego_zadania_Ministra_Edukacji_i_Nauki.2C_Krak.C3.B3w_.E2.80.93_marzec_2006_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Raport_z_realizacji_priorytetowego_zadania_Ministra_Edukacji_i_Nauki.2C_Krak.C3.B3w_.E2.80.93_marzec_2006-137">[137]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt><b>Population growth in Kraków since 1791</b></dt>
</dl>
<div class="timeline-wrapper"><map name="timeline_ad9932672434f2b3f6dcec9a440004ac"></map><img usemap="#timeline_ad9932672434f2b3f6dcec9a440004ac" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/timeline/ad9932672434f2b3f6dcec9a440004ac.png" /></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Krak%C3%B3w&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Churches_of_Krak%C3%B3w" title="Churches of Kraków">Churches of Kraków</a> and <a href="/wiki/Synagogues_of_Krak%C3%B3w" title="Synagogues of Kraków">Synagogues of Kraków</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wawel_katedra2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Wawel_katedra2.jpg/170px-Wawel_katedra2.jpg" width="170" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Wawel_katedra2.jpg/255px-Wawel_katedra2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Wawel_katedra2.jpg/340px-Wawel_katedra2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3057" data-file-height="3057" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wawel_katedra2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Wawel_Cathedral" title="Wawel Cathedral">Wawel Cathedral</a>, home to royal coronations and resting place of many national heroes; considered to be Poland's national sanctuary</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The metropolitan city of Kraków is known as the city of churches. The abundance of landmark, historic temples along with the plenitude of monasteries and convents earned the city a countrywide reputation as the "Northern Rome" in the past. The churches of Kraków comprise over 120 places of worship (2007) of which over 65 were built in the 20th century. More are still being added.<sup id="cite_ref-diecezja_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diecezja-138">[138]</a></sup> In addition to <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism">Roman Catholicism</a>, other denominations present include <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mariavite_Church" title="Mariavite Church">Mariavite Church</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polish_Catholic_Church" title="Polish Catholic Church">Polish Catholic Church</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polish_Orthodox_Church" title="Polish Orthodox Church">Polish Orthodox Church</a>, <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestantism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Latter-Day_Saints" class="mw-redirect" title="Latter-Day Saints">Latter-Day Saints</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Krak%C3%B3w_-_St._Mary_Church_01.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Krak%C3%B3w_-_St._Mary_Church_01.JPG/170px-Krak%C3%B3w_-_St._Mary_Church_01.JPG" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Krak%C3%B3w_-_St._Mary_Church_01.JPG/255px-Krak%C3%B3w_-_St._Mary_Church_01.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Krak%C3%B3w_-_St._Mary_Church_01.JPG/340px-Krak%C3%B3w_-_St._Mary_Church_01.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2126" data-file-height="3189" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Krak%C3%B3w_-_St._Mary_Church_01.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/St._Mary%27s_Basilica,_Krak%C3%B3w" title="St. Mary's Basilica, Kraków">Saint Mary's Basilica</a> (<i>Kościół Mariacki</i>)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Kraków contains also an outstanding collection of monuments of Jewish <a href="/wiki/Sacred_architecture" title="Sacred architecture">sacred architecture</a> unmatched anywhere in Poland. Kraków was an influential centre of Jewish spiritual life before the outbreak of World War II, with all its manifestations of religious observance from <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Judaism" title="Orthodox Judaism">Orthodox</a> to <a href="/wiki/Hasidic_Judaism" title="Hasidic Judaism">Chasidic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Reform_Judaism" title="Reform Judaism">Reform</a> flourishing side by side. There were at least 90 synagogues in Kraków active before the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_German" class="mw-redirect" title="Nazi German">Nazi German</a> invasion of Poland, serving its burgeoning Jewish community of 60,000–80,000 (out of the city's total population of 237,000), established since the early 12th century.<sup id="cite_ref-Dylewski_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dylewski-141">[141]</a></sup></p>
<p>Most synagogues of Kraków were ruined during World War II by the <a href="/wiki/Nazis" class="mw-redirect" title="Nazis">Nazis</a> who despoiled them of all ceremonial objects, and used them as storehouses for ammunition, firefighting equipment, as general storage facilities and stables. The post-<a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">Holocaust</a> Jewish population of the city had dwindled to about 5,900 before the end of the 1940s. Poland was the only <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">Eastern Bloc</a> country to allow free Jewish <a href="/wiki/Aliyah" title="Aliyah">aliyah</a> without visas or exit permits upon the conclusion of World War II.<sup id="cite_ref-D-H_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-D-H-142">[142]</a></sup> By contrast, Stalin forcibly kept Soviet Jews in the USSR, as agreed to in the <a href="/wiki/Yalta_Conference" title="Yalta Conference">Yalta Conference</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Kochavi-15_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kochavi-15-143">[143]</a></sup> In recent time, thanks to efforts of the local Jewish and Polish organisations including foreign financial aid from the <a href="/wiki/American_Jewish_Joint_Distribution_Committee" title="American Jewish Joint Distribution Committee">American Jewish Joint Distribution Committee</a>, many synagogues underwent major restorations and serve religious and tourist purposes.<sup id="cite_ref-jewish-guide_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jewish-guide-144">[144]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Krak%C3%B3w&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Krak%C3%B3w" class="mw-redirect" title="Education in Kraków">Education in Kraków</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Krakow_univesity_of_economics_main_building_cropped.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Krakow_univesity_of_economics_main_building_cropped.JPG/220px-Krakow_univesity_of_economics_main_building_cropped.JPG" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Krakow_univesity_of_economics_main_building_cropped.JPG/330px-Krakow_univesity_of_economics_main_building_cropped.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Krakow_univesity_of_economics_main_building_cropped.JPG/440px-Krakow_univesity_of_economics_main_building_cropped.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2242" data-file-height="1575" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Krakow_univesity_of_economics_main_building_cropped.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w_University_of_Economics" title="Kraków University of Economics">Kraków University of Economics</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Kraków is a major centre of education. Twenty-four institutions of higher education offer courses in the city, with more than 200,000 students.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> Jagiellonian University, the oldest university in Poland and ranked by the <i><a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education" title="Times Higher Education">Times Higher Education Supplement</a></i> as the second-best university in the country,<sup id="cite_ref-THES_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-THES-146">[146]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Jagiellonian_University_ranking_among_world_universities_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jagiellonian_University_ranking_among_world_universities-147">[147]</a></sup> was founded in 1364 as the Cracow University and renamed in 1817 to commemorate the Jagiellonian dynasty of <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth" title="Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth">Polish-Lithuanian</a> kings.<sup id="cite_ref-jagiellonian_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jagiellonian-148">[148]</a></sup> Its principal academic asset is the <a href="/wiki/Jagiellonian_Library" title="Jagiellonian Library">Jagiellonian Library</a>, with more than 4 million volumes, including a large collection of medieval manuscripts<sup id="cite_ref-Treasures_of_the_Jagiellonian_Library_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Treasures_of_the_Jagiellonian_Library-149">[149]</a></sup> like <a href="/wiki/Nicolaus_Copernicus" title="Nicolaus Copernicus">Copernicus</a>' <i><a href="/wiki/De_revolutionibus_orbium_coelestium" title="De revolutionibus orbium coelestium">De Revolutionibus</a></i> and the <a href="/wiki/Balthasar_Behem_Codex" title="Balthasar Behem Codex">Balthasar Behem Codex</a>. With 42,325 students (2005) and 3,605 academic staff, the Jagiellonian University is also one of the leading research centres in Poland. Famous historical figures connected with the University include <a href="/wiki/John_Cantius" title="John Cantius">Saint John Cantius</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jan_D%C5%82ugosz" title="Jan Długosz">Jan Długosz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nicolaus_Copernicus" title="Nicolaus Copernicus">Nicolaus Copernicus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andrzej_Frycz_Modrzewski" title="Andrzej Frycz Modrzewski">Andrzej Frycz Modrzewski</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jan_Kochanowski" title="Jan Kochanowski">Jan Kochanowski</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_III_Sobieski" title="John III Sobieski">King John III Sobieski</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pope_John_Paul_II" title="Pope John Paul II">Pope John Paul II</a> and Nobel laureates <a href="/wiki/Ivo_Andri%C4%87" title="Ivo Andrić">Ivo Andrić</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wis%C5%82awa_Szymborska" title="Wisława Szymborska">Wisława Szymborska</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Wislawa_Szymborska.2C_Nobel_Prize_in_Literature_1996_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wislawa_Szymborska.2C_Nobel_Prize_in_Literature_1996-150">[150]</a></sup></p>
<p>AGH University of Science and Technology, established in 1919, is the largest <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_technology" title="Institute of technology">technical university</a> in Poland, with more than 15 faculties and student enrollment exceeding 30,000.<sup id="cite_ref-AGH-UST_staff_and_students.2C_introduction_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AGH-UST_staff_and_students.2C_introduction-151">[151]</a></sup> It was ranked by the Polish edition of <i><a href="/wiki/Newsweek" title="Newsweek">Newsweek</a></i> as the best technical university in the country in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-agh_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-agh-152">[152]</a></sup> During its 80-year history, more than 73,000 students graduated from AGH with master's or bachelor's degrees. Some 3,600 persons were granted the degree of <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Science" title="Doctor of Science">Doctor of Science</a>, and about 900 obtained the qualification of <a href="/wiki/Habilitation" title="Habilitation">Habilitated Doctor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-History_of_AGH-UST_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_of_AGH-UST-153">[153]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Krak%C3%B3w,_Collegium_Maius_-_fotopolska.eu_(331634).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Krak%C3%B3w%2C_Collegium_Maius_-_fotopolska.eu_%28331634%29.jpg/220px-Krak%C3%B3w%2C_Collegium_Maius_-_fotopolska.eu_%28331634%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Krak%C3%B3w%2C_Collegium_Maius_-_fotopolska.eu_%28331634%29.jpg/330px-Krak%C3%B3w%2C_Collegium_Maius_-_fotopolska.eu_%28331634%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Krak%C3%B3w%2C_Collegium_Maius_-_fotopolska.eu_%28331634%29.jpg/440px-Krak%C3%B3w%2C_Collegium_Maius_-_fotopolska.eu_%28331634%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1250" data-file-height="833" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Krak%C3%B3w,_Collegium_Maius_-_fotopolska.eu_(331634).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i><a href="/wiki/Collegium_Maius" title="Collegium Maius">Collegium Maius</a></i>, Jagiellonian University's oldest building</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Other institutions of higher learning include <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Music_in_Krak%C3%B3w" title="Academy of Music in Kraków">Academy of Music in Kraków</a> first conceived as <a href="/wiki/College_or_university_school_of_music" class="mw-redirect" title="College or university school of music">conservatory</a> in 1888, one of the oldest and most prestigious conservatories in Central Europe and a major concert venue;<sup id="cite_ref-History_of_the_Akademia_Muzyczna_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_of_the_Akademia_Muzyczna-154">[154]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cracow_University_of_Economics" class="mw-redirect" title="Cracow University of Economics">Cracow University of Economics</a>, established in 1925;<sup id="cite_ref-Krak.C3.B3w_University_of_Economics_homepage_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Krak.C3.B3w_University_of_Economics_homepage-155">[155]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pedagogical_University_of_Cracow" class="mw-redirect" title="Pedagogical University of Cracow">Pedagogical University</a>, in operation since 1946;<sup id="cite_ref-Akademia_Pedagogiczna_w_Krakowie.2C_homepage_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Akademia_Pedagogiczna_w_Krakowie.2C_homepage-156">[156]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Agricultural_University_of_Cracow" class="mw-redirect" title="Agricultural University of Cracow">Agricultural University of Cracow</a>, offering courses since 1890 (initially as a part of <a href="/wiki/Jagiellonian_University" title="Jagiellonian University">Jagiellonian University</a>);<sup id="cite_ref-Akademia_Rolnicza.2C_homepage_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Akademia_Rolnicza.2C_homepage-157">[157]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jan_Matejko_Academy_of_Fine_Arts" title="Jan Matejko Academy of Fine Arts">Academy of Fine Arts</a>, the oldest <a href="/wiki/Fine_art" title="Fine art">Fine Arts</a> Academy in Poland, founded by the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Polish_painters" title="List of Polish painters">Polish painter</a> Jan Matejko; <a href="/wiki/Ludwik_Solski_Academy_for_the_Dramatic_Arts" title="Ludwik Solski Academy for the Dramatic Arts">Ludwik Solski Academy for the Dramatic Arts</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-krakow4_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-krakow4-158">[158]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pontifical_Academy_of_Theology" title="Pontifical Academy of Theology">The Pontifical Academy of Theology</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-Papieska_Akademia_Teologiczna.2C_homepage_in_English_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Papieska_Akademia_Teologiczna.2C_homepage_in_English-159">[159]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Cracow_University_of_Technology" class="mw-redirect" title="Cracow University of Technology">Cracow University of Technology</a>, which has more than 37,000 graduates.</p>
<p>Scientific societies and their branches in Kraków conduct scientific and educational work in local and countrywide scale. <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Learning" title="Academy of Learning">Academy of Learning</a>, Cracow Scientific Society, <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Law_Students%27_Library_of_the_Jagiellonian_University" title="Association of Law Students' Library of the Jagiellonian University">Association of Law Students' Library of the Jagiellonian University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polish_Copernicus_Society_of_Naturalists" title="Polish Copernicus Society of Naturalists">Polish Copernicus Society of Naturalists</a>, Polish Geological Society, Polish Theological Society in Kraków, Polish Section of <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Electrical_and_Electronics_Engineers" title="Institute of Electrical and Electronics Engineers">Institute of Electrical and Electronics Engineers</a> and Polish Society for Synchrotron Radiation have in Kraków their main seats.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Krak%C3%B3w&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Krak%C3%B3w" title="Culture of Kraków">Culture of Kraków</a>, <a href="/wiki/Events_in_Krak%C3%B3w" class="mw-redirect" title="Events in Kraków">Events in Kraków</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w_Old_Town" title="Kraków Old Town">Kraków Old Town</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Lady_with_an_Ermine.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/The_Lady_with_an_Ermine.jpg/170px-The_Lady_with_an_Ermine.jpg" width="170" height="222" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/The_Lady_with_an_Ermine.jpg/255px-The_Lady_with_an_Ermine.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/The_Lady_with_an_Ermine.jpg/340px-The_Lady_with_an_Ermine.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3488" data-file-height="4560" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Lady_with_an_Ermine.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Leonardo_da_Vinci" title="Leonardo da Vinci">Leonardo da Vinci</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Lady_with_an_Ermine" title="Lady with an Ermine">Lady with an Ermine</a></i> at <a href="/wiki/National_Museum,_Krak%C3%B3w" title="National Museum, Kraków">National Museum</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Kraków was named the official <a href="/wiki/European_Capital_of_Culture" title="European Capital of Culture">European Capital of Culture</a> for the year 2000 by the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-European_Capital_of_Culture_in_Poland_again_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-European_Capital_of_Culture_in_Poland_again-160">[160]</a></sup> It is a major attraction for both local and international tourists, attracting seven million visitors a year.<sup id="cite_ref-Basic_info_for_foreigners_in_Krakow_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Basic_info_for_foreigners_in_Krakow-161">[161]</a></sup> Major landmarks include the <a href="/wiki/Main_Market_Square,_Krak%C3%B3w" class="mw-redirect" title="Main Market Square, Kraków">Main Market Square</a> with <a href="/wiki/St._Mary%27s_Basilica,_Krak%C3%B3w" title="St. Mary's Basilica, Kraków">St. Mary's Basilica</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Sukiennice" class="mw-redirect" title="Sukiennice">Sukiennice Cloth Hall</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Wawel_Castle" title="Wawel Castle">Wawel Castle</a>, the <a href="/wiki/National_Museum,_Krak%C3%B3w" title="National Museum, Kraków">National Art Museum</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Zygmunt_(bell)" class="mw-redirect" title="Zygmunt (bell)">Zygmunt Bell</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Wawel_Cathedral" title="Wawel Cathedral">Wawel Cathedral</a>, and the medieval St Florian's Gate with the <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w_barbican" class="mw-redirect" title="Kraków barbican">Barbican</a> along the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Road,_Krak%C3%B3w" title="Royal Road, Kraków">Royal Coronation Route</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-krakow-info_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-krakow-info-162">[162]</a></sup> Kraków has 28 museums and <a href="/wiki/Public_art" title="Public art">public art</a> galleries. Among them is the <a href="/wiki/National_Museum,_Krak%C3%B3w" title="National Museum, Kraków">National Museum</a> featuring works by <a href="/wiki/Leonardo_da_Vinci" title="Leonardo da Vinci">Leonardo da Vinci</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rembrandt" title="Rembrandt">Rembrandt</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums_and_national_art_galleries">Museums and national art galleries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Krak%C3%B3w&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Museums and national art galleries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Krak%C3%B3w,_Gmach_G%C5%82%C3%B3wny_Muzeum_Narodowego_-_fotopolska.eu_(255212).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Krak%C3%B3w%2C_Gmach_G%C5%82%C3%B3wny_Muzeum_Narodowego_-_fotopolska.eu_%28255212%29.jpg/220px-Krak%C3%B3w%2C_Gmach_G%C5%82%C3%B3wny_Muzeum_Narodowego_-_fotopolska.eu_%28255212%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Krak%C3%B3w%2C_Gmach_G%C5%82%C3%B3wny_Muzeum_Narodowego_-_fotopolska.eu_%28255212%29.jpg/330px-Krak%C3%B3w%2C_Gmach_G%C5%82%C3%B3wny_Muzeum_Narodowego_-_fotopolska.eu_%28255212%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Krak%C3%B3w%2C_Gmach_G%C5%82%C3%B3wny_Muzeum_Narodowego_-_fotopolska.eu_%28255212%29.jpg/440px-Krak%C3%B3w%2C_Gmach_G%C5%82%C3%B3wny_Muzeum_Narodowego_-_fotopolska.eu_%28255212%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1400" data-file-height="933" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Krak%C3%B3w,_Gmach_G%C5%82%C3%B3wny_Muzeum_Narodowego_-_fotopolska.eu_(255212).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/National_Museum,_Krak%C3%B3w" title="National Museum, Kraków">National Museum</a> in Kraków is one of Poland's finest galleries of art</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Kraków's 28 museums are separated into the national and municipal museums; the city also has a number of art collections and public art galleries. The <a href="/wiki/National_Museum,_Krak%C3%B3w" title="National Museum, Kraków">National Museum</a>, established in 1879, as well as the National Art Collection on <a href="/wiki/Wawel_Hill" class="mw-redirect" title="Wawel Hill">Wawel Hill</a>, are all accessible to the general public and well patroned.</p>
<p>The National Art Collection is located at the <a href="/wiki/Wawel" title="Wawel">Wawel</a>, the former residence of three dynasties of Polish monarchs. Royal Chambers feature art, period furniture, Polish and European paintings, collectibles, and an unsurpassed display of the 16th-century monumental <a href="/wiki/Flemish_people" title="Flemish people">Flemish</a> <a href="/wiki/Tapestry" title="Tapestry">tapestries</a>. Wawel Treasury and Armoury features Polish royal memorabilia, jewels, applied art, and 15th to 18th century arms. The Wawel Eastern Collection features <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkish</a> tents and military accessories. The National Museum is the richest museum in the country with collections consisting of several hundred thousand items kept in big part in the Main Building at Ul. 3 Maja, although there are as many as eleven separate divisions of the museum in the city, one of the most popular being <a href="/wiki/Sukiennice_Museum" title="Sukiennice Museum">The Gallery of the 19th Century Polish Art in Sukiennice</a> with the collection of some of the best known paintings and sculptures of the <a href="/wiki/Young_Poland" title="Young Poland">Young Poland</a> movement. The latest division called <i>Europeum</i> with <a href="/wiki/Pieter_Brueghel_the_Younger" title="Pieter Brueghel the Younger">Brueghel</a> among a hundred Western European paintings was inaugurated in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-mkidn.gov.pl_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mkidn.gov.pl-163">[163]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Juliusz_S%C5%82owacki_Theatre,_Krak%C3%B3w.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Juliusz_S%C5%82owacki_Theatre%2C_Krak%C3%B3w.JPG/200px-Juliusz_S%C5%82owacki_Theatre%2C_Krak%C3%B3w.JPG" width="200" height="147" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Juliusz_S%C5%82owacki_Theatre%2C_Krak%C3%B3w.JPG/300px-Juliusz_S%C5%82owacki_Theatre%2C_Krak%C3%B3w.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Juliusz_S%C5%82owacki_Theatre%2C_Krak%C3%B3w.JPG/400px-Juliusz_S%C5%82owacki_Theatre%2C_Krak%C3%B3w.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2395" data-file-height="1766" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Kraków's renowned <a href="/wiki/Juliusz_S%C5%82owacki_Theatre" title="Juliusz Słowacki Theatre">Juliusz Słowacki Theatre</a>.</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:20110514_Krakow_Teatr_Slowackiego_9264.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/20110514_Krakow_Teatr_Slowackiego_9264.jpg/200px-20110514_Krakow_Teatr_Slowackiego_9264.jpg" width="200" height="126" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/20110514_Krakow_Teatr_Slowackiego_9264.jpg/300px-20110514_Krakow_Teatr_Slowackiego_9264.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/20110514_Krakow_Teatr_Slowackiego_9264.jpg/400px-20110514_Krakow_Teatr_Slowackiego_9264.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3963" data-file-height="2504" /></a></div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Other major museums of special interest in Kraków include the <a href="/wiki/Manggha" title="Manggha">Manggha</a> Museum of Japanese Art and Technology (at M. Konopnickiej 26),<sup id="cite_ref-Wyspia.C5.84ski_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wyspia.C5.84ski-164">[164]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Stanis%C5%82aw_Wyspia%C5%84ski" title="Stanisław Wyspiański">Stanisław Wyspiański</a> Museum (at 11 Szczepanska St),<sup id="cite_ref-Wyspia.C5.84ski_164-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wyspia.C5.84ski-164">[164]</a></sup> Jan Matejko Manor in Krzesławice,<sup id="cite_ref-Matejko_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Matejko-52">[52]</a></sup> – a museum devoted to the master painter and his life, Emeryk Hutten Czapski Museum,<sup id="cite_ref-Czapski_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Czapski-165">[165]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/J%C3%B3zef_Mehoffer" title="Józef Mehoffer">Józef Mehoffer</a> Manor.<sup id="cite_ref-Wyspia.C5.84ski_164-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wyspia.C5.84ski-164">[164]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Rynek Underground museum, under the main square, is an evocative modern display of Kraków's 1000+ years of history though its streets, activities and artifacts. This followed the massively extended excavations which started in a small way in 2005<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> and, as more and more was found, ran on eventually to 2010.</p>
<p>A half-an-hour tram-ride takes you to the little-heralded <a href="/wiki/Polish_Aviation_Museum" title="Polish Aviation Museum">Polish Aviation Museum</a> considered eighth world's best aviation museum by <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">CNN</a> and featuring over 200 aircraft including a <a href="/wiki/Sopwith_Camel" title="Sopwith Camel">Sopwith Camel</a> among other First World War biplanes; a comprehensive display of aero engines; and essentially a complete collection of airplane types developed by Poland after 1945.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> Activities of small museums around Kraków and in the Lesser Poland region are promoted and supported by the <a href="/wiki/Ma%C5%82opolska_Institute_of_Culture" title="Małopolska Institute of Culture">Małopolska Institute of Culture</a>; the Institute organises annual Małopolska Heritage Days.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Performing_arts">Performing arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Krak%C3%B3w&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Performing arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The city has several famous theatres, including the Narodowy Stary Teatr (the National Old Theatre),<sup id="cite_ref-Stary_Teatr_w_Krakowie.2C_homepage_in_Polish_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stary_Teatr_w_Krakowie.2C_homepage_in_Polish-169">[169]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Juliusz_S%C5%82owacki_Theatre" title="Juliusz Słowacki Theatre">Juliusz Słowacki Theatre</a>, the Bagatela Theatre, the <a href="/wiki/Ludowy_Theatre" title="Ludowy Theatre">Ludowy Theatre</a>, and the Groteska Theatre of Puppetry, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Opera_Krakowska" title="Opera Krakowska">Opera Krakowska</a> and Kraków Operetta. The city's principal concert hall and the home of the <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w_Philharmonic_Orchestra" title="Kraków Philharmonic Orchestra">Kraków Philharmonic Orchestra</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w_Philharmonic" title="Kraków Philharmonic">Kraków Philharmonic</a> (<i>Filharmonia Krakowska</i>) built in 1931.<sup id="cite_ref-KP_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KP-170">[170]</a></sup></p>
<p>Kraków hosts many annual and biannual artistic events,<sup id="cite_ref-krakow.pl-1_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-krakow.pl-1-171">[171]</a></sup> some of international significance such as the Misteria Paschalia (Baroque music), Sacrum-Profanum (contemporary music), the Cracow Screen Festival (<a href="/wiki/Popular_music" title="Popular music">popular music</a>), the Festival of <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Poland" title="Music of Poland">Polish Music</a> (classical music), Dedications (theatre), the <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w_Film_Festival" title="Kraków Film Festival">Kraków Film Festival</a> (one of Europe's oldest short films events),<sup id="cite_ref-Krakowski_Festiwal_Filmowy_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Krakowski_Festiwal_Filmowy-172">[172]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Etiuda%26Anima_International_Film_Festival" title="Etiuda&amp;Anima International Film Festival">Etiuda&amp;Anima International Film Festival</a> (the oldest international art-film event in Poland), Biennial of <a href="/wiki/Graphic_arts" title="Graphic arts">Graphic Arts</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Jewish_Culture_Festival" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish Culture Festival">Jewish Culture Festival</a>. Kraków was the residence of two Polish <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel</a> laureates in literature, <a href="/wiki/Wis%C5%82awa_Szymborska" title="Wisława Szymborska">Wisława Szymborska</a> and <a href="/wiki/Czes%C5%82aw_Mi%C5%82osz" title="Czesław Miłosz">Czesław Miłosz</a>; a third <a href="/wiki/List_of_Nobel_laureates" title="List of Nobel laureates">Nobel laureate</a>, the Yugoslav writer <a href="/wiki/Ivo_Andri%C4%87" title="Ivo Andrić">Ivo Andric</a>, lived and studied in Kraków. Other former longtime residents include internationally renowned <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Poland" title="Cinema of Poland">Polish film</a> directors <a href="/wiki/Andrzej_Wajda" title="Andrzej Wajda">Andrzej Wajda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roman_Polanski" title="Roman Polanski">Roman Polanski</a>, both of whom are <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Academy Award">Academy Award</a> winners.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Krak%C3%B3w&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Krak%C3%B3w_-_Filharmonia_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Krak%C3%B3w_-_Filharmonia_01.jpg/220px-Krak%C3%B3w_-_Filharmonia_01.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Krak%C3%B3w_-_Filharmonia_01.jpg/330px-Krak%C3%B3w_-_Filharmonia_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Krak%C3%B3w_-_Filharmonia_01.jpg/440px-Krak%C3%B3w_-_Filharmonia_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2474" data-file-height="1856" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Krak%C3%B3w_-_Filharmonia_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Concert hall of the <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w_Philharmonic" title="Kraków Philharmonic">Kraków Philharmonic</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Opera_Krakowska" title="Opera Krakowska">Opera Krakowska</a><sup id="cite_ref-krakowska_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-krakowska-173">[173]</a></sup> one of the leading national opera companies, stages 200 performances each year including ballet, operettas and musicals. It has, in its main repertoire, the greatest world and Polish opera classics. The Opera moved into its first permanent House in the autumn of 2008. It is in charge also of the <i>Summer Festival of Opera and Operetta</i>.</p>
<p>Kraków is home to two major Polish festivals of <a href="/wiki/Early_music" title="Early music">early music</a> presenting forgotten Baroque oratorios and operas: <i>Opera Rara</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-Opera_Rara_.E2.80.93_Krak.C3.B3w_.E2.80.93_8_December_2011_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Opera_Rara_.E2.80.93_Krak.C3.B3w_.E2.80.93_8_December_2011-174">[174]</a></sup> and <i>Misteria Paschalia</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-misteriapaschalia_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-misteriapaschalia-175">[175]</a></sup> Meanwhile, <a href="/wiki/Capella_Cracoviensis" title="Capella Cracoviensis">Capella Cracoviensis</a> runs the <i>Music in Old Cracow International Festival</i>.</p>
<p>Academy of Music in Kraków, founded in 1888, is known worldwide as the <i>alma mater</i> of the contemporary Polish composer <a href="/wiki/Krzysztof_Penderecki" title="Krzysztof Penderecki">Krzysztof Penderecki</a> and it is also the only one in Poland to have two winners of the <a href="/wiki/International_Chopin_Competition" class="mw-redirect" title="International Chopin Competition">International Chopin Competition</a> in Warsaw among its alumni. The Academy organises concerts of its students and guests throughout the whole year.<sup id="cite_ref-History_.E2.80.93_Cracow_Music_Academy_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_.E2.80.93_Cracow_Music_Academy-176">[176]</a></sup></p>
<p>Music organisations and venues include: Kraków Philharmonic,<sup id="cite_ref-krakow_fil_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-krakow_fil-177">[177]</a></sup> <i>Sinfonietta Cracovia</i> (a.k.a. the Orchestra of the Royal City of Kraków), the Polish Radio Choir of Kraków, <i>Organum</i> Academic Choir, the Mixed <a href="/wiki/Maria%C5%84ski_Choir" title="Mariański Choir">Mariański Choir</a> (<i>Mieszany Chór Mariański</i>), Kraków Academic Choir of the <a href="/wiki/Jagiellonian_University" title="Jagiellonian University">Jagiellonian University</a>, the Kraków Chamber Choir, <i>Amar Corde</i> String Quartet, <i>Consortium Iagellonicum</i> Baroque Orchestra of the <a href="/wiki/Jagiellonian_University" title="Jagiellonian University">Jagiellonian University</a>, Brass Band of T. Sendzimir Steelworks, and <i>Camerata</i> Chamber Orchestra of Radio Kraków.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Krak%C3%B3w&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>According to recent official statistics, in 2016 Kraków was visited by over 12 million tourists including 2.9 million foreign travelers. The visitors spent over 5.4 billion <a href="/wiki/Z%C5%82oty" class="mw-redirect" title="Złoty">złoty</a> (€1.2 billion) in the city (without travel costs and pre-booked accommodations). Most foreign tourists came from Great Britain, followed by German, Italian, Portuguese, Spanish, Canadian and American visitors.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup> The Kraków tour-guide from the Lesser Poland Visitors Bureau indicated that not all statistics are recorded due to considerable number of those who come, staying in readily available private rooms paid by cash, especially from Eastern Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-rp.pl.2F398262_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rp.pl.2F398262-179">[179]</a></sup></p>
<p>The main reasons for visiting the city are: its historical monuments, recreation as well as relatives and friends (placing third in the ranking), religion and business. There are 120 quality hotels in Kraków (usually about half full) offering 15,485 overnight accommodations.<sup id="cite_ref-intur.com_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-intur.com-180">[180]</a></sup> The average stay last for about 4 to 7 nights. The survey conducted among the travelers showed that they enjoyed the city's friendliness most, with 90% of Polish tourists and 87% foreigners stating that they would personally recommend visiting it.<sup id="cite_ref-rp.pl.2F398262_179-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rp.pl.2F398262-179">[179]</a></sup> Notable points of interest outside the city include the <a href="/wiki/Wieliczka_Salt_Mine" title="Wieliczka Salt Mine">Wieliczka salt mine</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Tatra_Mountains" title="Tatra Mountains">Tatra Mountains</a> 100&#160;km (62&#160;mi) to the south, the historic city of <a href="/wiki/Cz%C4%99stochowa" title="Częstochowa">Częstochowa</a> (north-west), the well-preserved former Nazi concentration camp at <a href="/wiki/Auschwitz-Birkenau_State_Museum" class="mw-redirect" title="Auschwitz-Birkenau State Museum">Auschwitz</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ojc%C3%B3w_National_Park" title="Ojców National Park">Ojcowski National Park</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Krakow_Day_Trips_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Krakow_Day_Trips-181">[181]</a></sup> which includes <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_in_Poland" title="Renaissance in Poland">the Renaissance</a> Castle at <a href="/wiki/Pieskowa_Ska%C5%82a" title="Pieskowa Skała">Pieskowa Skała</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Top_10_things_to_do_in_Krak.C3.B3w_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Top_10_things_to_do_in_Krak.C3.B3w-182">[182]</a></sup> Kraków has been awarded a number of top international rankings such as the 1st place in the <i>Top city-break destinations 2014</i> survey conducted by the British <i><a href="/wiki/Which%3F" title="Which?">Which?</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Krak%C3%B3w&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stadion_przed_meczem_z_APOELEM.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Stadion_przed_meczem_z_APOELEM.jpg/220px-Stadion_przed_meczem_z_APOELEM.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Stadion_przed_meczem_z_APOELEM.jpg/330px-Stadion_przed_meczem_z_APOELEM.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Stadion_przed_meczem_z_APOELEM.jpg/440px-Stadion_przed_meczem_z_APOELEM.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stadion_przed_meczem_z_APOELEM.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Wis%C5%82a_Krak%C3%B3w" title="Wisła Kraków">Wisła Kraków</a> Stadium</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Kraków was the host city of the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIVB_Men%27s_Volleyball_World_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="2014 FIVB Men's Volleyball World Championship">2014 FIVB Men's Volleyball World Championship</a> and <a href="/wiki/2016_European_Men%27s_Handball_Championship" title="2016 European Men's Handball Championship">2016 European Men's Handball Championship</a>. It has also been selected as the European City of Sport for 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-aktualnosci_2014_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aktualnosci_2014-184">[184]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> is one of the most popular sports in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-Krakow_Sport_Information_Guide_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Krakow_Sport_Information_Guide-185">[185]</a></sup> The two teams with the largest following are thirteen-time Polish champion <a href="/wiki/Wis%C5%82a_Krak%C3%B3w" title="Wisła Kraków">Wisła Kraków</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Wis.C5.82a_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wis.C5.82a-186">[186]</a></sup> and five-time champion <a href="/wiki/Cracovia_(football_club)" class="mw-redirect" title="Cracovia (football club)">Cracovia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Czarni_Pogo.C5.84_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Czarni_Pogo.C5.84-187">[187]</a></sup> both founded in 1906 as the oldest still existing in Poland.<sup id="cite_ref-skwk.pl_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-skwk.pl-188">[188]</a></sup> They have been involved in the most intense rivalry in the country and one of the most intense in all of Europe, known as the <a href="/wiki/Holy_War_(Krak%C3%B3w)" title="Holy War (Kraków)">Holy War</a> (<i><span lang="pl">Święta Wojna</span></i>).<sup id="cite_ref-footballderbies.com_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-footballderbies.com-189">[189]</a></sup> Other <a href="/wiki/Football_team" title="Football team">football clubs</a> include <a href="/wiki/Hutnik_Krak%C3%B3w" class="mw-redirect" title="Hutnik Kraków">Hutnik Kraków</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wawel_Krak%C3%B3w" title="Wawel Kraków">Wawel Kraków</a>, and one-time Polish champion <a href="/wiki/Garbarnia_Krak%C3%B3w" title="Garbarnia Kraków">Garbarnia Kraków</a>. There is also the first-league rugby club <a href="/wiki/Juvenia_Krak%C3%B3w" title="Juvenia Kraków">Juvenia Kraków</a>. Kraków has a number of additional, equally valued sports teams including twelve-time Polish <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a> champions <a href="/wiki/KS_Cracovia_(ice_hockey)" title="KS Cracovia (ice hockey)">Cracovia</a> and the twenty-time women's basketball champions Wisła Kraków.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stade_J%C3%B3zef_Pi%C5%82sudski.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Stade_J%C3%B3zef_Pi%C5%82sudski.jpg/220px-Stade_J%C3%B3zef_Pi%C5%82sudski.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Stade_J%C3%B3zef_Pi%C5%82sudski.jpg/330px-Stade_J%C3%B3zef_Pi%C5%82sudski.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Stade_J%C3%B3zef_Pi%C5%82sudski.jpg/440px-Stade_J%C3%B3zef_Pi%C5%82sudski.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stade_J%C3%B3zef_Pi%C5%82sudski.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/KS_Cracovia_(football)" title="KS Cracovia (football)">Cracovia</a> Stadium</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Cracovia_Marathon" title="Cracovia Marathon">Cracovia Marathon</a>, with over a thousand participants from two dozen countries annually, has been held in the city since 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-Marathon_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marathon-190">[190]</a></sup> Poland's first F1 racing driver <a href="/wiki/Robert_Kubica" title="Robert Kubica">Robert Kubica</a> was born and brought up in Kraków, as was former WWE tag team champion <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Putski" title="Ivan Putski">Ivan Putski</a>, and Top 10 ranked women's tennis player <a href="/wiki/Agnieszka_Radwa%C5%84ska" title="Agnieszka Radwańska">Agnieszka Radwańska</a>.</p>
<p>The construction of a new Kraków Arena began in May 2011; for concerts, indoor athletics, hockey, basketball, <a href="/wiki/Futsal" title="Futsal">futsal</a>, etc. The Arena will be ready in 2013; the total cost is estimated to be 363 million <a href="/wiki/Polish_z%C5%82oty" title="Polish złoty">Polish złoty</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The date of the event predicted near this tag has passed. (July 2017)">needs update</span></a></i>]</sup> It will accommodate up to 15 thousand viewers. In the case of a concert, when the stage is set on the lower arena, the facility will be able to seat up to 18 thousand people.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The date of the event predicted near this tag has passed. (July 2017)">needs update</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Kraków was <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w_bid_for_the_2022_Winter_Olympics" title="Kraków bid for the 2022 Winter Olympics">bidding</a> to host the <a href="/wiki/2022_Winter_Olympics" title="2022 Winter Olympics">2022 Winter Olympics</a> with <a href="/wiki/Jasn%C3%A1" title="Jasná">Jasná</a> but the bid was rejected by a majority (69.72%) of the vote in <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w_referendum,_2014" title="Kraków referendum, 2014">a referendum</a> on 16 May 2014. The referendum was organised after a wave of criticism from citizens who believed that the Olympics would not promote the city. The organizing committee of "Krakow 2022" spent almost $40,000 to pay for a citizen-approved logo, but many citizens considered this a waste of public money. The committee was rumoured to have fraudulently used several million zlotys for unknown expenses.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_relations">International relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Krak%C3%B3w&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: International relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_twin_towns_and_sister_cities_in_Poland" title="List of twin towns and sister cities in Poland">List of twin towns and sister cities in Poland</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Contemporary_foreign_names_for_the_city">Contemporary foreign names for the city</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Krak%C3%B3w&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Contemporary foreign names for the city">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Kraków is referred to by various names in different languages. The city is known in <a href="/wiki/Czech_language" title="Czech language">Czech</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovak_language" title="Slovak language">Slovak</a> and <a href="/wiki/Serbian_language" title="Serbian language">Serbian</a> as <i>Krakov</i>, in Hungarian as <span lang="hu"><i>Krakkó</i></span>, in <a href="/wiki/Lithuanian_language" title="Lithuanian language">Lithuanian</a> as <span lang="lt"><i>Krokuva</i></span>, in Finnish as <span lang="lt">"Krakova"</span>, in <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a> as <span lang="de"><i>Krakau</i></span>, in <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a>, Spanish and Italian as <span lang="la"><i>Cracovia</i></span>, in French as <span lang="fr"><i>Cracovie</i></span>, in <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> as <span lang="pt"><i>Cracóvia</i></span> and in Russian as Краков. <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_language" title="Ukrainian language">Ukrainian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yiddish_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Yiddish language">Yiddish</a> languages refer to it as <span lang="uk"><i>Krakiv</i></span> (Краків) and <span lang="yi"><i>Kroke</i> (קראָקע)</span> respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-krakow5_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-krakow5-191">[191]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Names_of_European_cities_in_different_languages:_I-L#K" class="mw-redirect" title="Names of European cities in different languages: I-L">Names of Kraków in different languages</a> are also available.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_towns_and_sister_cities">Twin towns and sister cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Krak%C3%B3w&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Twin towns and sister cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<li id="cite_note-The_Krak.C3.B3w_Ghetto_1940.E2.80.931943-64"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-The_Krak.C3.B3w_Ghetto_1940.E2.80.931943_64-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Bieberstein: Zagłada Żydów w Krakowie. Kraków 1985. J. Kast, B. Siegler, P. Zinke: Das Tagebuch der Partisanin Justyna. Jüdischer Widerstand in Krakau. Berlin 1999. Articles from Kraków newspapers (mostly from the local "<a href="/wiki/Gazeta_Wyborcza" title="Gazeta Wyborcza">Gazeta Wyborcza</a>") published in March 2003 on the 60th anniversary of the liquidation of the Kraków ghetto. Featuring historical maps. <cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.historyplace.com/worldwar2/holocaust/h-krak-beg.htm">"The Kraków Ghetto 1940–1943"</a><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">11 September</span> 2007</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AKrak%C3%B3w&amp;rft.btitle=The+Krak%C3%B3w+Ghetto+1940%E2%80%931943&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.historyplace.com%2Fworldwar2%2Fholocaust%2Fh-krak-beg.htm&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>

<tr>
<td colspan="2" class="navbox-list navbox-odd hlist" style="width:100%;padding:0px">
<div style="padding:0em 0.25em">
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Auschwitz_concentration_camp" title="Auschwitz concentration camp">Auschwitz-Birkenau</a> <small>German Nazi Concentration and Extermination Camp (1940–1945)</small></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bia%C5%82owie%C5%BCa_Forest" title="Białowieża Forest">Białowieża Forest / Belovezhskaya Pushcha</a> <small>(with <a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">Belarus</a>)</small></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Malbork_Castle" title="Malbork Castle">Castle of the Teutonic Order in Malbork</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Centennial_Hall" title="Centennial Hall">Centennial Hall, Wrocław</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Churches_of_Peace" title="Churches of Peace">Churches of Peace</a> <small>in Jawor and Świdnica</small></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w_Old_Town" title="Kraków Old Town">Cracow's Historic Centre</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kalwaria_Zebrzydowska_park" title="Kalwaria Zebrzydowska park">Kalwaria Zebrzydowska</a>: <small>the Mannerist Architectural and Park Landscape Complex and Pilgrimage Park</small></li>
